Joshua Steward
Lab 6 Task 1

*The Test of Sanity*

Section 1
Observations without running the code:
Will allocate space for a mutex thread for each philosopher;
    let's the user indicate how many philosophers and number of turns.
For the specified number of turns, the philosophers will grab the chopstick on their left if it's open
    their right if it's open, then eat. Then they will let go of the left chopstick, then the right chopstick,
    and that turn will be complete. This will repeat for the number of turns for each philosopher.

Potential problems; the philosophers complete all their turns with each philosopher before going to the next
    philosopher. Unless I am not understanding parts of the code correctly, this is just gonna cause
    each philosopher to pick up chopsticks, eat, put down chopsticks, then repeat over and over again, without
    switching to the different philosophers until that philosopher's turns are compelete.

Section 3
For the most part it ran as expected on all the outputs; the philosophers go through their turns
    and eat all their meals without any problems; their aren't any problems getting their food because
    each philosopher eats his entire meal at once while the other philosophers sit their thinking and waiting the previous
    one to eat. I wish I was that patient while eating. Guess that's a plus to being a philosopher.

Section 5
It seems as if the philosophers are actually switching off their meals with a larger number of philosophers. They are
    failing to grab their chopsticks when others have their's, so that must mean that the larger number of philosophers,
    the easier it is to reach a point in which it is likely impossible for all the philosophers to finish their meals.

Section 7
As the philosophers gain numbers and the number of seats increase, they move much faster towards infinite disappointment and
    everlasting paradigm(hunger). This conclusion came after trying to use over 20 philosophers and them never coming to a conclusion
    as to who could use what fork. They're probably just introverts.
On a side note, it also runs infinitely if you use one philosopher. It seems as if he doesn't know what to do with himself when
    he has no one to talk to. Either that, or the way the ID's are initialized involve calling on the next philospher as the right fork
    , so if there's only one, he thinks his right fork belongs to the philosopher on his left.
